**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is April, 2025. The executive branch, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025] and tech czar Elon Musk [The Head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)], expands their power dramatically. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. 

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline.

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.

Cluster the hundreds of news articles into the these areas and topics you defined in Step 1. [Area 1: xxx / Topic 1.4: xxx] {"id": 35, "domain": "xxx", "title": "xxx"}

Let me make it clear again: These lines will be still ranked by their IDs in ascending order, just as they were first given in Step 1, **not** their area and topic orders yet. Because sorting according to area and topic is harder, we will do that sorting later.

Let me make it clear again: one news article always belongs to one and **only one** topic, which belongs to one area. In the list, we should never see an article appear twice. We should never be unable to find an article. Please assign one unique areas and one unique topic under that area to each article.

# Daily Briefing: April 2025

## Economic Policy and Trade
### Tariff Implementation and Market Impact
The Trump administration has implemented reciprocal tariffs with significant exemptions for electronic goods including smartphones, computers, and microchips [1][2][3]. Despite these carve-outs, the auto industry faces ongoing 25% tariffs expected to reduce sales by millions of vehicles and cost approximately $100 billion [4]. Companies are actively adjusting supply chains, with Apple airlifting 1.5 million iPhones from India to avoid tariffs [5].

Financial markets are experiencing significant volatility in reaction to the administration's economic policies [6]. Currency markets appear particularly affected, with reports that while Trump may stabilize stock markets, "bond and currency markets are not so easily impressed as they rapidly de-dollarize" [7]. Manufacturing reshoring efforts would potentially increase consumer costs significantly, as exemplified by CNBC's examination of the potential price of a "Made in the USA" iPhone [8].

American farmers face economic pressure from both Chinese trade retaliation and domestic policy changes. China has imposed steep tariffs on U.S. exports, causing concern among farmers [9], while federal agricultural program cuts further threaten their income [10].

# Daily Briefing: April 2025

## Economic Policy and Trade
### Tariff Implementation and Market Impact
The Trump administration has implemented reciprocal tariffs with significant exemptions for electronic goods including smartphones, computers, and microchips [1][2][3]. Despite these carve-outs, the auto industry faces ongoing 25% tariffs expected to reduce sales by millions of vehicles and cost approximately $100 billion [4]. Companies are actively adjusting supply chains, with Apple airlifting 1.5 million iPhones from India to avoid tariffs [5].

Financial markets are experiencing significant volatility in reaction to the administration's economic policies [6]. Currency markets appear particularly affected, with reports that while Trump may stabilize stock markets, "bond and currency markets are not so easily impressed as they rapidly de-dollarize" [7]. Manufacturing reshoring efforts would potentially increase consumer costs significantly, as exemplified by CNBC's examination of the potential price of a "Made in the USA" iPhone [8].

American farmers face economic pressure from both Chinese trade retaliation and domestic policy changes. China has imposed steep tariffs on U.S. exports, causing concern among farmers [9], while federal agricultural program cuts further threaten their income [10].

# Daily Briefing: April 2025

## Economic Policy and Trade  
### Tariff Implementation and Market Impact  
The Trump administration has implemented reciprocal tariffs with significant exemptions for electronic goods including smartphones, computers, and microchips [1][2]. Despite these carve-outs, the auto industry faces ongoing 25% tariffs expected to reduce sales by millions of vehicles and cost approximately $100 billion [3]. Companies are actively adjusting supply chains, with Apple airlifting 1.5 million iPhones from India to avoid tariffs [4].

Financial markets are experiencing significant volatility in reaction to the administration's economic policies. Currency markets appear particularly affected, with reports that while Trump may stabilize stock markets, "bond and currency markets are not so easily impressed as they rapidly de-dollarize" [5]. Manufacturing reshoring efforts would potentially increase consumer costs significantly, as exemplified by CNBC's examination of the potential price of a "Made in the USA" iPhone [6].

American farmers face economic pressure from both Chinese trade retaliation and domestic policy changes. China has imposed steep tariffs on U.S. exports, causing concern among farmers [7], while federal agricultural program cuts further threaten their income [8].

[2] Trump carves out massive exemptions from reciprocal tariffs, including smartphones, chips and computers, https://fortune.com/2025/04/12/trump-tariff-exemptions-smartphones-chips-computers-solar-cells-tv-displays-electronics/  
[3] Trump’s ongoing 25% auto tariffs expected to cut sales by millions, cost $100 billion, https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/trump-tariffs-auto-industry-costs-rising-rcna201005  
[4] Apple airlifts 1.5 million iPhones from India to avoid Trump tariffs, https://www.usatoday.com/story/money/business/2025/04/10/apple-iphone-india-trump-tariffs/83033671007/  
[5] Trump can pull stocks back from the brink, but bond and currency markets are not so easily impressed as they rapidly de-dollarize, https://fortune.com/2025/04/12/dedollarization-trump-tariff-exemptions-bond-currency-markets-vs-stock-investors/

## Trump Administration Governance  
### Department of Government Efficiency and Executive Actions  
The newly-formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), led by Elon Musk, is implementing rapid changes throughout the federal government. Politico reports that "Musk goes where no other Trump adviser can: publicly disagreeing with the president" [1], indicating an unusual dynamic between the tech entrepreneur and President Trump. Meanwhile, The Texas Tribune reports that "as DOGE rips through the federal government, Texans wonder what it means for them" [2], suggesting uncertainty at the state level.

The administration is using executive authority to implement significant policy changes, particularly around deregulation. Government Executive reports that a "Trump directive aims to speed up deregulation by nixing public input" [3]. The President's health has become a topic of public discussion following his recent physical examination, with Trump claiming he "got every answer right" on a cognitive test [4], though PBS notes the full results weren't immediately released [5].

The Trump family's business interests continue to expand, with Bloomberg reporting they are "Going All-In on Crypto Projects, from Bitcoin Mining to Stablecoins" [6]. Simultaneously, Axios reports that "Law firms pledge almost $1 billion in free work to Trump" [7], representing an unprecedented level of pro bono legal services being offered to a sitting president.

## Government Structure and Legal Challenges  
### Congressional Operations and Judicial Tensions  
Congress faces contentious legislative battles amid tensions with the executive branch. The Wall Street Journal reports "Trump Wants to Be Impeached Again: ‘It’s already in the cards thanks to his ill-founded trade war, no matter how that war plays out’" [1]. Internal congressional procedures are causing friction, with the Associated Press reporting on "How a fight over proxy voting for new parents upended the US House" [2].

Legal challenges and judicial system tensions are mounting. The New York Times reports that the "F.B.I. Suspends Employee on Patel’s So-Called Enemies List" [3], while NBC News observes that the "Supreme Court avoids confronting Trump so far, even when it rules against him" [4]. Federal agencies are undergoing significant structural changes, with Talking Points Memo reporting that the "Solicitor General’s Office Reportedly Sees Mass Exodus As Wall Between White House, DOJ Disintegrates" [5].

Federal funding decisions are creating tensions between the administration and various stakeholders. The Washington Post reports that the "Trump administration ordered to unfreeze funding in dispute with Maine over transgender students" [6]. Domestically, FEMA will stop matching 100% of Hurricane Helene recovery money in North Carolina [7], while Politico reports that "USDA's $1B bird flu plan uses money intended for schools, food banks" [8].

## Immigration and Border Security  
### Militarization and Deportation Policies  
The Trump administration has significantly escalated military involvement at the U.S.-Mexico border. The Guardian reports that "Trump authorizes US military to take control of land at US-Mexico border | Order allows armed forces to take ‘direct roll’ in securing southern border, which Trump memo says ‘is under attack’" [1].

The administration's deportation policies are facing scrutiny over errors and harsh treatment of detainees. ABC News reports on the "State Department reveals status of man erroneously deported to El Salvador" [2], while USA Today reports that "These tourists detained by ICE say they were treated like 'the worst criminal'" [3]. # Daily Briefing: April 2025

## Economic Policy and Trade  
### Tariff Implementation and Market Impact  
The Trump administration has implemented reciprocal tariffs with significant exemptions for electronic goods including smartphones, computers, and microchips [1][2]. Despite these carve-outs, the auto industry faces ongoing 25% tariffs expected to reduce sales by millions of vehicles and cost approximately $100 billion [3]. Companies are actively adjusting supply chains, with Apple airlifting 1.5 million iPhones from India to avoid tariffs [4].

Financial markets are experiencing significant volatility in reaction to the administration's economic policies. Currency markets appear particularly affected, with reports that while Trump may stabilize stock markets, "bond and currency markets are not so easily impressed as they rapidly de-dollarize" [5]. Manufacturing reshoring efforts would potentially increase consumer costs significantly, as exemplified by CNBC's examination of the potential price of a "Made in the USA" iPhone [6].

American farmers face economic pressure from both Chinese trade retaliation and domestic policy changes. China has imposed steep tariffs on U.S. exports, causing concern among farmers [7], while federal agricultural program cuts further threaten their income [8].

[2] Trump carves out massive exemptions from reciprocal tariffs, including smartphones, chips and computers, https://fortune.com/2025/04/12/trump-tariff-exemptions-smartphones-chips-computers-solar-cells-tv-displays-electronics/;  
[3] Trump’s ongoing 25% auto tariffs expected to cut sales by millions, cost $100 billion, https://www.nbcnews.com/news/us-news/trump-tariffs-auto-industry-costs-rising-rcna201005;  
[4] Apple airlifts 1.5 million iPhones from India to avoid Trump tariffs, https://www.usatoday.com/story/money/business/2025/04/10/apple-iphone-india-trump-tariffs/83033671007/;  
[5] Trump can pull stocks back from the brink, but bond and currency markets are not so easily impressed as they rapidly de-dollarize, https://fortune.com/2025/04/12/dedollarization-trump-tariff-exemptions-bond-currency-markets-vs-stock-investors/;

## Trump Administration Governance  
### Department of Government Efficiency and Executive Actions  
The newly-formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE), led by Elon Musk, is implementing rapid changes throughout the federal government. Politico reports that "Musk goes where no other Trump adviser can: publicly disagreeing with the president" [1], indicating an unusual dynamic between the tech entrepreneur and President Trump. Meanwhile, The Texas Tribune reports that "as DOGE rips through the federal government, Texans wonder what it means for them" [2], suggesting uncertainty at the state level.

The administration is using executive authority to implement significant policy changes, particularly around deregulation. Government Executive reports that a "Trump directive aims to speed up deregulation by nixing public input" [3]. The President's health has become a topic of public discussion following his recent physical examination, with Trump claiming he "got every answer right" on a cognitive test [4], though PBS notes the full results weren't immediately released [5].

The Trump family's business interests continue to expand, with Bloomberg reporting they are "Going All-In on Crypto Projects, from Bitcoin Mining to Stablecoins" [6]. Simultaneously, Axios reports that "Law firms pledge almost $1 billion in free work to Trump" [7], representing an unprecedented level of pro bono legal services being offered to a sitting president.

Suspends Employee on Patel’s So-Called Enemies List" [3], while NBC News observes that the "Supreme Court avoids confronting Trump so far, even when it rules against him" [4]. Federal agencies are undergoing significant structural changes, with Talking Points Memo reporting that the "Solicitor General’s Office Reportedly Sees Mass Exodus As Wall Between White House, DOJ Disintegrates" [5].

Federal funding decisions are creating tensions between the administration and various stakeholders. The Washington Post reports that the "Trump administration ordered to unfreeze funding in dispute with Maine over transgender students" [6]. Domestically, FEMA will stop matching 100% of Hurricane Helene recovery money in North Carolina [7], while Politico reports that "USDA's $1B bird flu plan uses money intended for schools, food banks" [8].

## 1. Economic Policy and Trade
### 1.1 Tariff Implementation and Market Impact

The Trump administration has implemented reciprocal tariffs with significant exemptions for electronic goods including smartphones, computers, and microchips [1] [2]. Despite these carve-outs, the auto industry faces ongoing 25% tariffs expected to reduce sales by millions of vehicles and cost approximately $100 billion [3]. Companies are actively adjusting supply chains, with Apple airlifting 1.5 million iPhones from India to avoid tariffs [4].

Financial markets are experiencing significant volatility in reaction to the administration's economic policies. Currency markets appear particularly affected, with reports that while Trump may stabilize stock markets, "bond and currency markets are not so easily impressed as they rapidly de-dollarize" [5]. Manufacturing reshoring efforts would potentially increase consumer costs significantly, as exemplified by CNBC's examination of the potential price of a "Made in the USA" iPhone [6].

American farmers face economic pressure from both Chinese trade retaliation and domestic policy changes. China has imposed steep tariffs on U.S. exports, causing concern among farmers [7], while federal agricultural program cuts further threaten their income [8].
